NOTICE to Stockholders of Honolulu 'Planta-
tion Company.â Notice is hereby given that in
pursuance of a resolution of the Board of Di-
rectors of the Honolulu Plantation Company,
duly adopted at a meeting of Said board held
en the 22d day of October, A. D. 190L a spe-
cial meeting of the stockholders of the Hono-
lulu Plantation Company will be held on
THURSDAY, the 26th day of December.
A. D. 1901, at the hour of 11 o'clock a. m. of
that day. at the office of the corporation. No.
S27 Market street, in the City and County of
San Francisco, State of California, the same
being the principal place of business and the
office of said corporation and the building
where the Beard jof Directors usually meet,
for the purpose of considering and acting
upon a proposition to create a bonded indebt-
edness of said corporation to the amount of
one million two hundred and fifty thousand
($1,250,000) dollars, to the end and for the
purpose of providing means and raising
moneys to pay the existing indebtedness of
said corporation and the indebtedness incurred
and to be incurred in the development of its
properties and the construction and comple-
tion of its works and improvements, the pur-
chase of machinery and the acquisition of
such other property* as may be within the
purposes and objects of said corporation.
H. W. THOMAS.
Secretary of Honolulu Plantation Company.
Dated San Francisco. October 22, 190L

TOPEKA, Kans., Oct. 28.â Hugh Wal
lace, aged 35 years, was shot and fatally
wounded by his aged father to-day. The
elder Wallace went to Oklahoma at the
time of the opening and persuaded his
son to go down and try for a claim. Not
drawing any, young- Wallace returned to
Topeka after spending quite a sum of
money. This caused bad feeling between
the men and the tragedy resulted.
Aged Father Shoots His Son.
The only reference of general Interest
was the promise that measures should
shortly be submittted to finally complete
the reform of the-currency.

THE ladies and gentlemen con
nected with Sacred Heart parish
will produce the pretty comic
opera, "The Doctor of Alcantara,"
"A Billionaire" was written by Peter
Robertson, a Bohemian Club man. There
are eight characters in the sketch, and
the text Is said to be bubbling over with
witty lines and clever situations.
Orrin Peck will play the part of a girl,
fair and only 17 and full of wisdom. Dr.
J. Wilson Shiels is the billionaire, who in
the development of the play is discovered
to be a fakerâ a "billoinaire" in his mind
only. J. C. Wilson runs through the play
as an "oil boomer"; Charles : Dickman is
Snapps, an artist; Dick Hotallng will play
the part of a tramp, and Beverly Letcher
a servant. There is "also a "policeman"
in the cast, but his identity off the stage
has not yet been disclosed.
The clubmen are having frequent re
hearsals, and those who have been priv
ileged to attend them declare that in this
sketch they are going to surpass even the
splendid record they have .previously es
tablished.
Unusual interest is being manifested in
the skit, "A Billionaire," in which' the
Bohemian Club men will appear. The
talent and versatility of the brilliant club
men are a well established fact, but the
public has never been allowed to revel in
it The Bohemian heretofore . has sung
and played and danced and quipped his
jokes to the delight and. for the delight of
his fellow clubmen only. The doll show
will be the first time that Bohemian talent
may be seen and enjoyed outside the'sa
cred precincts of Bohemian Clubdom.
the grand doll show to be held, at
the Palace Hotel on the 8th and 9th of
November.

DAUGHTERS BUSY
WITH SHOW PLANS
Mrs. Blair and Miss Jennie Blair are
preparing to leave their Van Ness avenue
home and to go to- the' Richelieu," where
they intend to pass "the" winter. "
Mr. and "Mrs. : Joseph S. Tobln have
taken the Blair home on "Van Ness avenue
and will move in on November L
Thirty ladies enjoyed a delightful after
noon at a euchre party at the home of
Mrs. Foute yesterday afternoon. Six ta
bles were ranged in the drawing rooms,
which were gay with bright blossoms, and
a warmly contested gauie was played.
The hours were from 2 till. 6. .After the
game there was a dainty service of re
freshments and an hour; spent in pleasant
conversation.
Apropos of golfing, news comes via New
York that the Brookline Country Club,
which has an excellent 18-hole course, is
preparing to make a strong bid for the
women's national championship next year.
The excellent showing of the Boston
women on the New Jersey links, although
disappointed in not winning the leading
honor, will be used as a strong argument
in favor of the move. The qualifying six
teen included seven members of clubs In
or near Boston, and they also showed up
well in the consolation set. Miss Elizabeth
Porter of the Oakley Club winning the
cup. The Brookline Club has always
taken a prominent part in the encourage
ment of women's golf, and holds an open
tournament for the fair players every
year.
SMALL and altogether exclusive
will be the meetings of the Fri
day Fortnlghtlys this winter. The
dancing class will meet six times
and the opening cotillon will be
held on the evening of November 22. As
usual, the meetings will take place at
Cotillon Hall and are to "be characterized
by the Eame delightful - informality and
early hours that made the Fortnlghtlys
to vastly popular during last winter. The
Christmas meeting, as has # heretofore been
the custom, will be an army and navy
cotillon.
At the first cotillon nearly all the de
butantes will be present. I know that
Miss Catherine Robinson, Miss Pearl Zan
ders. Miss Annie Foster and Miss Frances
licKinetry are going and that all these
charming buds anticipate a most delight
ful season.
I am inclined to believe that of all these
dainty debutantes Miss Catherine Robin
son will be the most sought after. She is
a graceful maid, with bright eyes and
glowing cheeks, and a manner that every
one is going to find vecy hard to resist.
Miss Robinson Is the daughter of C. P.
Kobiireon and a niece of Mrs. Jarboe and
Mrs. Monroe Salisbury.
The demands for cards to the Fort
nightlys have been eo great and the hall
accommodations are so liraited that no out
side invitations will be issued this year.
When the class was first organized invita
tions were restricted to the visiting lists
of the original patronesses, Mrs. Ira
Pierce, Mrs. Gordon Blanding and Mrs.
Monroe Salisbury. These same lists will
this year govern the sending out of invi
tations.
